272881

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT, by Gwendolyn D. Clemons,
Director, transmitting a Communication, dated August 16, 2005:
Re:

Falcon Investment Holdings, LLC
Resolution Approving Class 8 Special Exception to Abandonment

respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding the Falcon Investment Holdings, LLC's
application for a Class 8 property tax incentive for your consideration.
Falcon Investment Holdings, LLC requests approval of the special exception to the 24
month abandonment rule under the Class 8 Ordinance. This Resolution is required so
that the company can complete its application to the Assessor of Cook County.
Submitting Falcon Investment Holdings, LLC's application for a Class 8, the Ordinance
of the Village of Park Forest, Illinois, and a Department of Planning and Development
staff report for your information.

3136

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDfNGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners had adopted a Real Property
Assessment Classification 8 that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level
for a an industrial facility; and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an
application from Falcon Investment Holdings, LLC and the Resolution from the Village
of Park Forest for an abandoned industrial facility located at 70 North Street, Park Forest,
Cook County, Illinois, PIN numbers 31-25-207-018, 019, 020, 021 , 022 and 047; and
WHEREAS, Class 8 requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period
of qualifying abandonment in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for
less than 24 consecutive months upon purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building
was abandoned for 15.5 months at the time of application, and that special circumstances
are present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of
Commissioners of the County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of
Commissioners indicate their approval for the filing of an application for a Cook County
Real Estate Classification 8 abatement incentive to the company for an abandoned
industrial facility located at 70 North Street, Park Forest, Cook County, lllinois, under the
provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and
directed to forward a certified copy of this resolution to the Office of the Cook County
Assessor.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that Communication No. 272881
be discharged from the Committee on Business and Economic Development. The motion to discharge
carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Collins, moved that Communication No. 272881
- Appl ication for Class 8 Special Exception to Abandonment from Falcon Investment Holdings, LLC be
approved. The motion carried.
Commissioners Claypool and Gorman voted present on the above item.

AUTHORJZATJON TO DISCHARGE COMMUNICATION NO. 270513
FROM COMMITTEE ON BUSINESS AND ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated October 3, 2005 from
ROBERTO MALDONADO, County Commissioner
requesting that Communication No. 2705 I 3, a Resolution requiring the Assessor's Office to provide an
annual report to the Board listing the estimated assessed value and the estimated exempt dollar amount of
each non-profit hospital in Cook County beginning with the current year's tri-annual reassessment, be
discharged from the Tax and Revenue Subcommittee that was refe rred at the April 6, 2005 meeting.
I further request that this matter be referred to the Finance Committee for immediate consideration.
2705 13

RESOLUTION TO PROVIDE AN ANNUAL REPORT TO THE BOARD LISTING THE
ESTIMATED ASSESSED VALUE AND THE ESTIMATED EXEMPT DOLLAR
AMOUNT OF EACH NON-PROFIT HOSPITAL IN COOK COUNTY BEGINNING
WITH THE CURRENT YEAR'S TRI-ANNUAL REASSESSM ENT (PROPOSED
RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Roberto Maldonado,
County Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by Joan Patricia Murphy, County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, over seventy non-profit hospitals benefit from property tax exemptions in Cook
County and have a moral, fina ncial and legal responsibility to provide quality health care to
the poor and uninsured; and

3138

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

WHEREAS, in June of 2005, non-profit hospitals will begin filing an annual report known
as a "Community Benefits Plan," in accordance with state law which will include the amount
of charity care and other community benefits the hospital provides; and
WHEREAS, in addition to receiving exemptions from Cook County property taxes (which
according to independent research accounts for approximately 20% of the total annual value
of the hospital's preferential tax status), non-profit hospitals in Cook County also may receive
exemptions from various federal and state income taxes, state and local sales and use taxes,
tax-exempt bond financing, and tax-deductible donations; and
WHEREAS, in order to qualify for property tax exempt status in Cook County, the property
utilized by the non-profit hospital must be exclusively used in a charitable manner, as
detennined by the Illinois Department of Revenue during its review of certificates of
exemption; and
WHEREAS, currently, the Assessor's Office cannot calculate an approximate assessed value
for tax exempt non-profit hospitals and, therefore, there is no information to gauge the
monetary savings non-profit hospitals accrue through their tax exempt status; and
WHEREAS, unlike a typical homeowner who receives an exemption based on a percentage
of the home' s assessed value through the Homeowner's Exemption, a non-profit hospital
receives a total exemption from the hospital's assessed value; and
WHEREAS, in order to fairly and accurately weigh the monetary value of the non-profit
hospitals' property tax exemption against the dollar amount given back to the community
through charity care and other community benefits, it is necessary to analyze the hospital ' s
Community Benefits Plan along with a report from the Assessor's Office that details each
hospital's estimated assessed value and the estimated exempt dollar amount.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
does hereby require the Cook County Assessor's Office to provide an annual report to the
Board listing the estimated assessed value and the estimated exempt dollar amount of each
non-profit hospital in Cook County beginning with the current year's tri-annual reassessment.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that communication be
discharged from the Tax and Revenue Subcommittee. The motion to discharge carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Communication No.
270513 - Resolution to provide an annual report to the Board listing the estimated assessed value and the
estimated exempt dollar amount of each non-profit hospital in Cook County beginning with the current
year's tri-annual reassessment, be referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 270513). The
motion carried.
Commissioner Goslin voted "no" on the above item.

3139

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENTS
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
FORREST CLAYPOOL and LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioners
Co-Sponsored by
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT

AMENDMENT TO THE RULES OF ORGANIZATION AND PROCEDURE ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners annually presents an Executive
Budget Recommendation to the Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners debates and considers the budget, debates and considers
relevant amendments, and passes a budget for Cook County by the end of February of each calendar year;
and
WHEREAS, in the past the Board of Commissioners has usually had fewer than four months to review
an annual budget that funds over 25 ,000 FTE positions and contains $3 billion in revenues and
expenditures and therefore cannot give appropriate consideration to each aspect of the budget; and
WHEREAS, given the large fiscal deficits that have arisen over the past several years and have needed to
be filled by the President and the Board of Commissioners, and further given the differences of opinions
with regard to closing the deficits, it is important that all parties have adequate time to consider the
budget, write and propose amendments, and arrive at an ultimate decision to either support or oppose the
budget recommendation; and
WHEREAS, recognizing the need for a specified and uniform budgeting process, the U.S. Congress
passed the Congressional Budget and Impoundment Control Act of 1974, which still forms the basis for
the budget process; and
WHEREAS, the Congressional Budget and lmpoundment Control Act species that the President of the
United States is to transmit his or her budget to Congress on or after the first Monday in January but not
later than the first Monday in February of each year for the following fiscal year, which begins on
October 1, thereby giving Congress eight months to review and act on the President's recommendation;
and
WHEREAS, all governments should be seeking to involve citizens in budgeting and legislating, allowing
for greater time before the presentation of the budget and the ensuing consideration by the Board will
allow for more citizens to make their voices heard and for the President and the Board of Commissioners
to better seek out the opinions of their constituents; and
WHEREAS, Cook County currently has no set date by which the President must provide the Executive
Budget Recommendation to the Board of Commissioners.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that the Cook County Rules of Organization and Procedure
Ordinance is hereby amended as set forth below:

3140

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

ARTICLE III
BUDGET MATTERS

3-1.

Finance Committee.

(a)
The President's executive budget recommendations and all motions, resolutions or
ordinances that propose, amend, transfer or supplement any appropriations of funds or budget measure
shall be referred to the Finance Committee. The executive budget recommendations shall provide the
basis upon which the annual appropriation ordinance is prepared and enacted~, and it will be presented to
the Finance Committee on or after September 15 but no later than October 15 for the fiscal year that
begins in December of that calendar year.
(b)
After considering the executive budget recommendations submitted by the President and
all other budget measures submitted by members, the Finance Committee shall prepare an annual
appropriation ordinance in tentative form, which in such tentative fonn shall be made conveniently
available to public inspection for at least ten ( l 0) days prior to final action thereon, by publication in the
journal of the proceedings of the Board or in such other form as the Board may prescribe; and not less
than one week after publication of such tentative appropriation bill and prior to final action thereon, the
Finance Committee shall hold at least one public hearing thereon, notice of which shall be given by
publication in a newspaper having general circulation in the County at least one week prior to the time of
such hearing. It shall be the duty of the Finance Committee to prepare such tentative appropriation bill
and make it so available to public inspection and also to arrange for and hold such public hearing or
hearings.

Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Claypool, moved that the Proposed Ordinance
Amendment be referred to the Committee on Finance.
Following discussion, Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to amend
the motion and send the Proposed Ordinance Amendment to the Committee on Rules. (Comm. No.
273415). The motion carried unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
FORREST CLAYPOOL and LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioners
Co-Sponsored by
ANTHONY J . PERAICA, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT

AMENDMENT TO THE RULES OF ORGANIZATION AND PROCEDURE ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, allowing the public, media, and civic groups, as well as the Board of Commissioners,
access to the Comprehensive Annual Financial Report (CAFR) at the soonest possible date after the close
of the fiscal year makes the County' s finances more accountable to the public; and

3141

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

WHEREAS, delaying the release of the CAFR in a timely manner diminishes the accountability of the
County because important and final information regarding the health of the budget and the County's
spending is withheld from the public; and
WHEREAS, the last CAFR released by the County for Fiscal Year 2003 was not released until February
17, 2005, or 14.5 months after the close of the fiscal year, and the CAFR for Fiscal Year 2002 was not
released until March 31, 2004, or 16 months after the close of the fiscal year; and
WHEREAS, the other large governments within Cook County, the City of Chicago, the Chicago Public
Schools, the Chicago Park District, and the Metropolitan Water Reclamation District, and the Forest
Preserve District of Cook County, released their CAFRs within six months of the fiscal year; and
WHEREAS, the budgets of the Chicago Public Schools (CPS) and the City of Chicago are far larger than
the Cook County's, and therefore, the work of the CPS and the City show that it is possible to release
CAFRs for large, complicated budgets within six months of the close of the fiscal ; and
WHEREAS, there is currently no set date by which Cook County must release its Comprehensive
Annual Financial Report.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that the Cook County Rules of Organization and Procedure
Ordinance is hereby amended as set forth below:

ARTICLE III
BUDGET MATTERS
3-1.

Finance Committee.

(a)
The President's executive budget recommendations and all motions, resolutions or
ordinances that propose, amend, transfer or supplement any appropriations of funds or budget measure
shall be referred to the Finance Committee. The executive budget recommendations shall provide the
basis upon which the annual appropriation ordinance is prepared and enacted.
(b)
After considering the executive budget recommendations submitted by the President and
all other budget measures submitted by members, the Finance Committee shall prepare an annual
appropriation ordinance in tentative fom1, which in such tentative form shall be made conveniently
available to public inspection for at least ten (I 0) days prior to final action thereon, by publication in the
journal of the proceedings of the Board or in such other form as the Board may prescribe; and not less
than one week after publication of such tentative appropriation bill and prior to final action thereon, the
Finance Committee shall hold at least one public hearing thereon, notice of which shall be given by
publication in a newspaper having general circulation in the County at least one week prior to the time of
such hearing. It shall be the duty of the Finance Committee to prepare such tentative appropriation bill
and make it so available to public inspection and also to arrange for and hold such public hearing or
hearings.

{f}
For Fiscal Year 2005 forward. the Comprehensive Annual Financial Report for the Cook
County government will be released to the Board and the public no later than May 31 of the following
calendar year, or within six months of the close of the fiscal year. This means that the CAFR for Fiscal
Year 2005 will be released by May 3 1, 2006.

3142

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Claypool, moved that the Proposed Ordinance
Amendment be referred to the Committee on Finance.
Following discussion, Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to amend
the motion and send the Proposed Ordinance Amendment to the Committee on Rules. (Comm. No.
273416). The motion carried unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
FORREST CLAYPOOL and LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioners
Co-Sponsored by
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT

AMENDMENT TO THE RULES OF ORGANIZATION AND PROCEDURE ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners annually presents a budget to
the Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, due to the current manner in which the budget is presented, it is difficult for the Board of
Commissioners to see the prevailing trends in revenue collection, expenditures, and the size of the overall
budget; and
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners usually has fewer than four months to review an annual budget
that funds over 25,000 FTE positions and contains $3 billion in revenues and expenditures; and
WHEREAS, it serves the interests of any form of government, including Cook County, to plan its
revenue and expenditures several years in advance in order to allow more preparation for future budget
negotiations as well as to allow for a macroscopic view of the budget situation over the next several years;
and
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners' having a macroscopic view of the budget situation over
several years benefits Cook County by allowing for the Board to consider the impacts on future budgets
when making adjustments to the revenue or expenditure streams; and
WHEREAS, all governments should be seeking ways to involve citizens further in budgeting and
legislating, and making multi-year projections freely available to the public encourages participation and
allows residents and businesses to have more infonnation regarding future taxes and services; and
WHEREAS, many local governments across the nation, as well as the State of Virginia, have mandated
through their laws that their budget departments publish six-year revenue and expenditure projections;
and

3143

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDfNGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

WHEREAS, the Civic Federation, a non-partisan government research organization, has long called on
Cook County to make revenue projections available to the Board of Commissioners and the public; and
WHEREAS, The National Advisory Council on State and Local Budgeting (NACSLB) and the
Government Finance Officers Association (GFOA) both recommend that all governments formally adopt
a long-tenn financial plan as a key component of a sound budget process, including the projection of
multi-year revenue trends and modeling of various revenue and expenditure options that is shared with
and/or reviewed by key policymakers and stakeholders; and
WHEREAS, Cook County does not currently publish revenue and expenditure projections in advance
and doing so would confonn to a highly-regarded budgetary practice.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that the Cook County Rules of Organization and Procedure
Ordinance is hereby amended as set forth below:
ARTICLE III
BUDGET MATTERS

3-1.

Finance Committee.

(a)
The President' s executive budget recommendations and all motions, resolutions or
ordinances that propose, amend, transfer or supplement any appropriations of funds or budget measure
shall be referred to the Finance Committee. The executive budget recommendations shall provide the
basis upon which the annual appropriation ordinance is prepared and enacted .

.(Q}
In addition to the executive budget recommendations, the President will present to the
Finance Committee revenue and expenditure projections for the next six fiscal years. The projection of
revenue will be itemized into the categories of Property Tax Leyy, Intergovernmental Transfer, Home
Rule Taxes, Other Revenues, Fees, and Fund Balance; and the projection of expenditures will be itemized
into the categories of Public Safety, Bond and Interest, Corporate, Allowance for Taxes, Health, Other,
Capital, Annuity, and Grants. The six-year fiscal projection will also be accompanied by a narrative text
which lists and explains the assumptions made in order to reach the revenue and expenditure projections.

W ill
After considering the executive budget recommendations submitted by the President and
all other budget measures submitted by members, the Finance Committee shall prepare an annual
appropriation ordinance in tentative form, which in such tentative form shall be made conveniently
available to public inspection for at least ten (10) days prior to final action thereon, by publication in the
journal of the proceedings of the Board or in such other fonn as the Board may prescribe; and not less
than one week after publication of such tentative appropriation bill and prior to final action thereon, the
Finance Committee shall hold al least one public hearing thereon, notice of which shall be given by
publication in a newspaper having general circulation in the County at least one week prior to the time of
such hearing. It shall be the duty of the Finance Committee to prepare such tentative appropriation bill
and make it so available to public inspection and also to arrange for and hold such public hearing or
hearings.

3144

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Claypool, moved that the Proposed Ordinance
Amendment be referred to the Committee on Finance.
Following discussion, Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to amend
the motion and send the Proposed Ordinance Amendment to the Committee on Rules. (Comm. No.
273417). The motion carried unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, DEBORAH SIMS and PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
AMENDMENT OF SECTION 8.7.1 OF THE
COOK COUNTY ZONING ORDINANCE OF 2001
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS
that Section 8.7.l of the Cook County Zoning Ordinance of2001 be amended as follows:
8.7.1

FENCES, WALLS, HEDGES AND SHRUBBERY
A.

Fences, walls, hedges and shrubbery may be erected, placed, maintained or grown within
ten ( 10) feet of a lot line on property abutting or located in a residential district unless
otherwise provided in Section 8.4. The height of a fence, wall, hedge or shrubbery shall not
exceed six (6) feet above ground level and, if located in a required front or corner side yard,
shall not exceed a height of three (3) feet.

B.

Fences, walls, hedges and shrubbery shall not be erected, placed, maintained or grown
within five (5) feet of a lot line on any non-residential zoned property in excess of ten (10)
feet in height.

C.

Fences, walls, hedges and shrubbery shall not be erected, constructed, maintained or grown
to a height exceeding three (3) feet above the street grade when located within thirty-five
(35) feet of the right-of-way line.

D.

Fences shall be constructed so that the poles, suppo11 and braces are on the inside of the
fence of the property being fenced and so that the " good" side of the fence is facing
neighboring property (unless otherwise approved by the Building Commissioner).

Commissioner Gonnan, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Proposed Ordinance
Amendment be referred to the Committee on Zoning and Building. (Comm. No. 273418). The motion
carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE COUNTY ASSESSOR
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Transmitting a Communication, dated September 16, 2005 from
JAMES M. HOULIHAN, Cook County Assessor
respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding the support of the 7% Expanded Homeowner
Exemption for your consideration.
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
JOHN P. DALEY and LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioners
Co-Sponsored by
FORREST CLAYPOOL, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, PETER N. SILVESTRI,
PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR., JERRY BUTLER, EARLEAN COLLINS,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE QUIGLEY, DEBORAH SIMS and BOBBIE L. STEELE, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, homeowners in Cook County are overburdened by the overwhelming increases in property
value, as evidenced most particularly in the last three triennial reassessments; and
WHEREAS, due to the ever-increasing property tax burden, many long time residents are unable to
remain in the prospering neighborhoods they helped to create; and
WHEREAS, the triennial reassessment cycle makes it difficult for Cook County homeowners to predict
and financially prepare for the impact of three years worth of property value increases in each
reassessment period; and
WHEREAS, many residents in gentrifying neighborhoods are so burdened by property taxes that they are
forced to lobby against neighborhood improvements, fearing the subsequent increases in their tax bills;
and
WHEREAS, increases in the median income of Cook County residents has not kept pace with the
dramatic increases in property values; and
WHEREAS, the overall burden of property taxes has steadily been shifting more and more onto owners
of residential properties; and
WHEREAS, the continuation of the Expanded Homeowner Exemption which essentially caps
assessment increases at 7% annually would continue to provide Cook County homeowners with
predictability and affordability, while also providing protection to our neighborhoods, encouraging
diversity and stability.

3147

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board does wholeheartedly support
the continuation of the 7% Expanded Homeowner Exemption and encourages the state to act swiftly to
renew this important property tax reform; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Members of the Cook County Board of Commissioners do
hereby urge the Illinois General Assembly and the Governor to make the 7% limitation on the increase in
taxable value of a homeowner's property permanent; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk deliver suitable copies of this Resolution to the
Governor of the State of Illinois, the President of the Illinois Senate, the Minority Leader of the Illinois
Senate, the Speaker of the Illinois House of Representatives and the Minority Leader of the Illinois House
of Representatives as a sign of our concern for this important issue.

Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 273419). The motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

by
JACK KELLY, Chief Financial Officer
requesting authorization to apply for a grant in the amount of $31,280.00 from the Illinois Department of
Transportation, Division of Traffic Safety. The purpose of this grant is to provide funds to hire back
officers during the Mini-Grant Alcohol Enforcement Program. During this detail, certified officers
working overtime will conduct enforcement campaigns related to impaired driving traffic laws. In
addition, the campaign also includes a preliminary public infonnation and education campaign, as well as
a post enforcement media release on subsequent results.

September 30, 2006.

Financial Officer of the Sheriff s Office be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

requesting authorization to accept a no-cost grant extension from the U.S. Department of Justice
(USDOJ), Office of Juvenile Justice Delinquency Prevention for the Cook County Internet Crimes
Against Children (ICAC) Task Force Program. This extension will enable the office to expend the entire
award amount as well as accomplish all of the program goals and objectives.
This grant provides funding to equip and train the Cook County ICAC Task Force partner agencies in an
effort to aggressively identify, investigate and prosecute persons who use the Internet to sexually exploit
children. The Cook County ICAC Task Force partners include representatives to the State's Attorney's
Office, the Chicago Police Department and law enforcement agencies from each of the five suburban
Municipal Districts. Task Force partners from local law enforcement agencies will concentrate their
investigative efforts in the City of Chicago and the entire outlying suburban Cook County area.
The authorization to accept the original grant was given on July 12, 2005 by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners in the amount of $100,000.00.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Funding period extension: October 1, 2005 through July 31, 2006.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the request of the Chief of
the Administrative Services Bureau of the State's Attorney's Office be approved. The motion carried
unanimously.
GRANT RENEW AL APPLICATION

Transmitting a Communication, dated September 16, 2005 from
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State's Attorney 's Office
requesting authorization to apply for a grant renewal in the amount of $ 142,338.00 from the Illinois
Criminal Justice Information Authority (ICJJA). The grant will provide one (1) year of funding for four
(4) positions dedicated to the Prosecutor Based Victim Assistance Services - Juvenile Court Program.
Specifically, the grant funds three (3) delinquency courtroom specialists and one (1) transfer specialist
who work in the Victim Assistance Program at Juvenile Court.

3172

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

This grant requires that the office match 25% of the grant award. The match commitment for this
program consists of both cash and in-kind contributions. The in-kind match fully supports the salary and
fringe benefits of one (1) of the juvenile court victim specialists. The cash match consists of the
remaining fringe benefits of the three (3) federally funded juvenile court specialists not covered by the
grant award.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $80,557.00 [$37,583.00 - (250-1 10 Account); $12,424.00 - (250-1 70/ 179
Account); and $30,550.00 - (250-818 Account)]. Grant Award: $142,338.00. Funding period:
December 19, 2005 through December 18, 2006.
Approval of this item would commit Fiscal Year 2006 funds.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the request of the Chief of
the Administrative Services Bureau of the State's Attorney's Office be approved. The motion carried
unanimously.

05-0-43
ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING THE COOK COUNTY ZONING ORDINANCE
REZONING CERTAIN PROPERTY LOCATED IN
HANOVER TOWNSHIP
WHEREAS, the owner of certain property located in Hanover Township, described in Section 1 herein,
has petitioned the Cook County Board of Commissioners to have the property reclassified from the C- 1
Restricted Business District to the C-4 General Commercial District fo r a real estate and employment
office; and

3 191

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

WHEREAS, the said petition was received by the Zoning Board of Appeals of the County of Cook, as
Docket #78 15, and a public hearing was held in regard to said request, after due notice, all in accordance
with the Cook County Zoning Ordinance and the Statutes of the State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the Zoning Board of Appeals entered detailed findings in accordance with the standards set
forth in the Cook County Zoning Ordinance recommending that the Cook County Board of
Commissioners grant said application for amendment; and
WHEREAS, it is the opinion of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that said property be
rezoned and reclassified in accordance with the recommendations of the Zoning Board of Appeals.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois:
Section 1: That the following described property be and the same is hereby rezoned from its C-1
Restricted Business District to the C-4 General Commercial District for a real estate and
employment office.
LEGAL DESCRIPTION
Of that part of the SW 1/4 of the SW 1/4 of Sec. 26, Township 41 North, Range 9, East of the
3rd Principal Meridian, described by beginning at a point in the South line of said Section 26,
3 19.91 ft. West of the SE comer of the SW 1/4 of the SW 1/4 of Section 26, and running
thence West along the South line thereof 152.75 ft. ; thence North 10 degrees 53 minutes East
175.68 ft. , to the center line of public road (Lake Street, U.S. Route 20); thence SE' ly along
said center line 151.20 ft.; thence South 10 degrees 53 minutes West 127.82 ft. to the place of
beginning.
commonly described as approximately 0.87 acre, located on the south side of Lake Street, approximately
500 feet east of Oak A venue in Hanover Township.
Section 2:

That Zoning Map 6 of the Cook County Zoning Ordinance, Cook County Comprehensive
Plan, and all other pertinent records be and the same shall be changed to show the rezoning of
the described property, hereby incorporated by reference into this Ordinance, as provided by
law.

Section 3: That this Ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after its passage and approval.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of October 2005.

STATE'S ATTORNEY, Richard A. Devine, submitting communication advising the County

Person, Hany Morkos, and Hany Morkos Individually, Case No. 04-L-7331. This case
alleging medical negligence has been settled for the sum of $35,000,000.00, which is within
the authority granted to this office by the Finance Committee' s Subcommittee on Litigation at
its September 7, 2005 meeting. The County will be responsible for the payment of
$20,000,000.00 of the settlement. Two insurance companies providing excess coverage to
the County, as set forth below, will pay the remaining $ 15,000,000.00. We have negotiated a
settlement that will be satisfied by payments in the 2005 and 2006 fiscal periods. Upon
approval, please prepare an initial check in the amount of $4,000,000.00 payable to The
Private Bank and Trust Company, Hany Morkos, and Pavalon, Gifford, Laatsch and Marino,
their attorneys.
On January I 0, 2006, Max Re, provider of the first layer of the County's excess insurance,
will pay $10,000,000.00 directly to the plaintiff, thus exhausting its entire limit. On January
10, 2006, the County will pay an additional $2 I ,000,000.00. $ I 6,000,000.00 of that payment
will satisfy the remaining portion of its self-insured retention obligation of $20,000,000.00
under our contracts of insurance, and $5,000,000.00 will be reimbursed to the County by XL,
provider of the second layer of the County' s excess insurance. Although the contract allows
XL thirty days to reimburse the County, we have successfully negotiated an agreement
whereby they will wire-transfer that payment to the County that same day. We will send a
letter directly to the Comptroller in regard to the second payment on or about January I, 2006
specifying the payout. Please forward the initial check to Mary Jo Smerz, Assistant State' s
Attorney, Medical Litigation Section, for transmittal.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON BUSINESS AND ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT
September 21, 2005
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Collins and Commissioner Quigley (2)

Absent:

Vice Chainnan Goslin, Commissioners Gonnan, Hansen, Maldonado and Murphy (5)

Also Present:

Commissioner Suffredin (I); Dr. Francis S. Muthu - Director, President's Office of
Employment Training (POET); and Charles L. Jenrich - Vice President of U.S.
Operations, GBJD Registrars

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Business and Economic Development of the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County met pursuant to notice on Wednesday, September 21, 2005 at the hour of I 0:00 A.M. in the Board
Room, Room 569, County Building, 11 8 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee as considered the following item for informational purposes only:
The Subcontracts of the Workforce Investment Act Grant from the Illinois Department of Commerce and
Economic Development, which was approved at the September 8, 2005 Board Meeting, Agenda Item
# 120.
The Secretary to the Board infonned the Chairman that a quorum was not present.
Chairman Collins replied that the meeting was being held for informational purposes only.
Chairman Collins stated in 2004 the County appropriated approximately $ 15 million to the POET
Program for job training and development. As Chairman of the Business and Economic Development
Committee, she has never seen the perfonnance data. The federal government was concerned about
maintaining the POET Program because of performance not only in Illinoi s but across the Country.
Chairman Collins said she is concerned about the high number of unemployed and unskilled individuals
in economically depressed communities. Funds should be allocated specifically to job training programs
that offer a potential job upon completion. The rate of unemployment is about 60%; this contributes to
the growth of the underworld drug culture within these communities.
Commissioner Suffredin asked how often the agencies receive grant money.

3251

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

Dr. Francis S. Muthu, Director, President's Office of Employment Training (POET), replied that the
funding is for a two year cycle. Further, Dr. Muthu stated that the President's Office of Employment
Training has put together an evaluation summary of 2004 placements which is a snap shot of May
because the Workforce Investment Board did not meet in July. The funding was received in August from
the State; performance of all the contractors was evaluated after May and presented to the Workforce
Investment Board (WIB). The WIB reviewed and recommended either full funding, provisional funding
or no funding. The provisional funding was recommended because the WIB had to look at the June
performance which is the end of POET's fiscal year. Dr. Muthu also stated that last year the second
installment of funding did not take place until January, therefore the contractors were given an additional
fiscal quarter to meet perfonnance. The WIB looked at the June data and looked at the end of the first
quarter of this fiscal year, and if the contractors are moving towards the perfonnance minimum which is
the job placement of 75% and above, then the contractors' funding would be renewed; if not they would
still be placed in conditional status until December.
Chainnan Collins called upon the agencies present.

273068

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNfNG AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated September I, 2005.
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing Agent
to advertise for bids for the Sheriff's Department of Women 's Justice Services Center Project.
It is respectfully requested that this Honorable Body approve this request.
Reason:

This project will provide for the construction of a new one story 1 1,000 square
foot facility at the Department of Corrections Campus, to be used by the Sheriff's
Department of Women's Justice Services to provide counseling and adult
education programs to the women under its supervision. LEED certification for
new buildings will also be included in the scope of this project.

The work will be split into two bid packages. Bid Package #I will include the design/build
construction services for the center. Bid Package #2 will include all of the freestanding
furniture.
Bond Issue (20000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

Randolph M. Johnston - Assistant State's Attorney, State's Attorney 's Office; Daniel H.

County; Gregg Cygan, R .Ph. - Director, Clinic Pharmacies, Walgreen' s Health Services;

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Health and Hospitals of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant
to notice on Wednesday, September 28, 2005 at the hour of 11 :30 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569,
County Building, 11 8 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following items and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:

3255

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

272042

RESOLUTION REGARDING DEVELOPMENT OF AN ALTERNATIVE METHODS
DEMONSTRATION PROJECT (PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed
Resolution sponsored by Gregg Goslin and Mike Quigley, County Commissioners; and Cosponsored by Carl R. Hansen, Anthony J. Peraica, Elizabeth Ann Doody Gorman and Peter
N. Silvestri, County Commissioners.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

PROJECT TO SUPPLEMENT BUREAU OF HEALTH'S PHARMACIES
WHEREAS, county residents utilizing the Bureau of Health Services in-house phannacies
routinely wait for hours to get prescriptions fi lled; and
WHEREAS, the Bureau of Health Services and the Cook County Board of Commissioners
continue to look for methods of more efficient delivery of prescriptions that will alleviate the
chronic wait for medications; and
WHEREAS, Stroger Hospital of Cook County is a qualified 340B covered entity and
therefore eligible to take part in an Alternative Methods Demonstration Project; and
WHEREAS, the Alternative Methods Demonstration Project gives covered entities a process
to obtain approval, through the Office of Pharmacy Affairs, to utilize a network of
phannacies or use a contract pharmacy to supplement an in-house pharmacy; and
WHEREAS, Walgreens Health Services has approached the County following the passage
on October 5, 2004 of a Resolution authorizing an RFP for pharmacy services. Walgreen's is
confident in their ability to develop an Alternative Methods Demonstration Project and to
provide effective methods to improve access to drug therapy and comprehensive pharmacy
services for patients while protecting the program integrity with inventory and dispensing
controls and ensuring statutory and program compliance; and
WHEREAS, Wal greens said one option is to establish a small network of their stores, chosen
by zip codes, to serve as 340B contract pharmacies to provide convenient, alternative
locations for patients in addition to the existing county phannacies; and
WHEREAS, Walgreens has also proposed an option to acquire the operation of the Stroger
Hospital of Cook County outpatient pharmacy providing the County with revenue and taking
over staffing responsibility, system maintenance and upgrade costs.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
instructs the Bureau of Health Services to enter into talks with WalgreeBs Health Seri.ices
various Pharmacy Administrators including all the companies listed in attachment #2 to
discuss an Alternative Methods Demonstration Project and the various options to be included
in that project; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Bureau of Health Services submit a draft of an
Alternative Methods Demonstration Project for the Board of Commissioners review by
September 20, 2005 January 27, 2006.
*Referred to the Health and Hospitals Committee on 07/12/05.

3256

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

Vice Chainnan Goslin stated that in response to his earlier legislation to possibly outsource the County's
pharmacy needs, Walgreen's submitted a letter to him outlining what they will provide to the County. In
order to adequately consider the above item, the Committee needs testimony from Walgreen 's explaining
their letter. Vice Chairman Goslin has distributed this letter. (The referenced document is on file in the
Office of the County Clerk).
Commissioner Collins asked whether other phannacies will have the opportunity to make proposals to the
Commissioners. Chairman Butler replied in the affinnative.
Chairman Butler called on Gregg Cygan, R.Ph., Director, Clinic Pharmacies, Walgreen' s Health Services,
to address the Commissioners.
Mr. Cygan thanked the Board for the opportunity to address questions and concerns. He stated that
Walgreen's goal is to ensure that Hospital patie nts receive adequate, quality care. In its proposal,
Walgreen' s focused on the Alternative Methods Demonstration Project. This arrangement would allow
Stroger Hospital of Cook County to offload some of the prescriptions to nearby Walgreen's pharmacies;
the result would be that acute as well as non-acute patients would receive timely service. Walgreen's is
open to assisting the County in other ways, for example by analyzing current operations.
Vice Chainnan Goslin stated for the record that in his conversations with Mr. Cygan, he explained that if
this program were to move -forward, a request for proposal would be issued, and the bidding process
would be open to other phannacies. Mr. Cygan concurred.
Vice Chainnan Goslin stated that the Bureau of Health Services will need to address the financial risk
involved in contracting with outside phannacies.
Mr. Cygan replied that Walgreen's is willing to help analyze both the financial impact and the work flow
impact of Walgreen's project.
Commissioner Quigley inquired about the volume of offload that the demonstration project can handle.
Mr. Cygan replied that this would depend on the number of designated phannacies, and this number has
not been deten11ined by the County, nor by Walgreen' s. The zip code distribution of patients would be
analyzed. Patients on Medicaid and other insurances would be able to use any phan11acies. All
calculations would be submitted to the Office of Phannacy Affairs.
Commissioner Quigley inquired as to how many prescriptions are not picked up at the phan11acies.
Mr. Cygan replied that every day, Walgreen ' s determines which prescriptions have not been picked up by
checking all prescriptions that are seven days and older. These prescriptions are deleted from any billings
to private insurances or Medicaid. The prescriptions are then returned to stock. He estimated that one
percent of the prescriptions are not picked up.
Commissioner Daley stated the following concerns: Possible revenue loss for Stroger Hospital of Cook
County, offloading prescriptions could possibly adversely affect Medicaid and Medicare patients; and the
resolution names Walgreen' s only, perhaps it should be amended to include other pharmacies.
Commissioner Gorman asked how Walgreen' s would handle the surge in prescriptions.
Mr. Cygan replied that the most important factor would be to determine how many patients reside in
which zip codes. Then Walgreen' s could designate the necessary additional staffing.

3257

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

County would incur.
Mr. Cygan replied that at this point he is not prepared to provide this information. He needs to analyze
the scope of the work. Two components of thi s analysis would be the pure filling of the prescription and,
with regard to the request for information (RFl) the administrative, and behind-the-scenes cost.

Mr. Cygan replied that he is not certain, because he was not directly involved.

Chairman Butler asked Dr. Daniel H. Winship, Chief, Bureau of Health Services, to address the
Committee.
Dr. Winship stated that after his remarks he will call on Daniel Martin, Deputy Chief, Bureau of Health
Services; Dr. Martin has been responsible for developing the Demonstration Project Program.
Dr. Winship stated that the report that was distributed to the Commissioners resulted from the Board
action in September of 2004. At this time the Bureau of Health Services was asked to seek a request for
proposal (RFP); ultimately this was corrected to a request for infonnation. The request for infomrntion
received only one response; therefore, the Bureau of Health Services contacted all of the phannacy
organizations for responses. A meeting resulted, during which cost infonnation was obtained.
Mr. Martin made the following presentation:
Because an RFI was issued, and not an RFP, the County was careful in soliciting cost infonnation.
However, parameters were requested for the following: the cost of filling prescriptions, the cost of
dispensing prescriptions for patients whose care would be uncompensated, and the cost for those patients
not covered under public aid or any other fonn of insurance. Walgreen's and CVS (also known as
Pharmacare) offered a combined cost range from $10 to $ 14.

3258

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

Mr. Martin continued that when the Bureau of Health Services was directed to issue the RFI , the issue
was raised regarding whether the County would be able to preserve its 340B purchasing rights; a
demonstration project is the means by which 340B purchasing rights are conveyed to a contracted
organization. A discussion ensued regarding the fact that the regulations allow for contracting with only
one individual site pharmacy. At that point the Commissioners directed the Bureau of Health Services to
talk with the Office of Pharmacy Affairs. In July Mr. Martin attended the 340B conference, where he met
with Mr. Mitchell, the Director of the Office of Pharmacy Affairs.
Mr. Martin further stated that Mr. Mitchell advised him that there were no public health systems in the
country currently authorized to conduct this type of program under a demonstration project. Currently
only single or double site, federally qualified, health-center clinics contract with either one or two
phannacies within a certain local. Mr. Mitchell indicated that, if Cook County elected to submit a
proposal, the Office of Phannacy Affairs would look favorably on it; it potentially could increase their
assets. However, the Office of Phamrncy Affairs had three concerns: One, the arrangement would have
to preserve the integrity of the 340B program; were the County to fail to do this, the program itself could
be in jeopardy, and other 340B entities could suffer. Two, the County would have to prove that there
would be an increase in access to the patients. And three, the County wou ld need to contain cost as a
result of doing a demonstration project.
Mr. Martin continued that an individual from Mr. Mitchell 's office walked him through the requirements
for submitting a demonstration project. The County and a contractor would file the application jointly.
The Office of Pharmacy Affairs would entertain an application only from the County to request a
demonstration project. If the application were granted, the County could put out a bid. The 340B aspect
could be addressed at this point.
Mr. Martin continued that recently the Bureau of Health Services has been able to bill for public aid
The County receives a flat-rate, enhanced
medications under the Intergovernmental Transfer.
reimbursement to help offset the cost of uncompensated phannacy care. The Bureau of Health Services
has had numerous discussions with the Illinois Department of Public Aid to determine whether the
County can preserve this revenue; while the Illinois Department of Public Aid does not appear amenable,
it has agreed to further review this issue. The Intergovernmental Transfer Agreement does not allow for
an arrangement whereby a contractor bills the County for Public Aid patients and then the County
submits claims on behalf of those Public Aid patients; the State Plan Amendment requires that all services
be rendered at one of the critical care sites, i.e., one of the three County Hospitals. The State indicated
that their average reimbursement is approximately $ 13.00 per prescription for generic drugs, and
approximately $80.00 per prescription for brand-name drugs. All patients who purchase prescriptions
from contracted phannacies would be required to pay the Illinois Department of Public Aid a co-pay.
ln conclusion, Mr. Martin offered the following analysis of the current cost for the County to provide
prescriptions. In 2004 the cost to the County was calculated to be $5.56 per prescription. Approximately
11 % to 13% of the patients are Public Aid patients. Approximately 80% of the patients are self-paid or
on uncompensated care. If the County were to contract with outside phannacies, it would be responsible
for paying any services not covered under any type of insurance program .

take part in an Alternative Methods Demonstration Project; and
WHEREAS, the Alternative Methods Demonstration Project gives covered entities a process to obtain
approval, through the Office of Phannacy Affairs, to utilize a network of phannacies or use a contract
phannacy to supplement an in-house pharmacy; and
WHEREAS, Walgreens Health Services has approached the County followi ng the passage on October 5,
2004 of a Resolution authorizing an RFP for pharmacy services. Walgreen's is confident in their ability
to develop an Alternative Methods Demonstration Project and to provide effective methods to improve
access to drug therapy and comprehensive phannacy services for patients while protecting the program
integrity with inventory and dispensing controls and ensuring statutory and program compliance; and
WHEREAS, Walgreens said one option is to establish a small network of their stores, chosen by zip
codes, to serve as 340B contract pharmacies to provide convenient, alternative locations for patients in
addition to the existing county pharmacies; and

WHEREAS, Walgreens has also proposed an option to acquire the operation of the Stroger Hospital of
Cook County outpatient phannacy providing the County with revenue and taking over staffing
responsibility, system maintenance and upgrade costs.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners instructs
the Bureau of Health Services to enter into talks with WalgreeRs Health Ser.iees various Pharmacy
Administrators including all the companies listed in attachment #2 to discuss an Alternative Methods
Demonstration Project and the various options to be included in that project; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Bureau of Health Services submit a draft of an Alternative
Methods Demonstration Project for the Board of Commissioners review by Se13tember 20, 2005 January
27, 2006.

272043

AMENDMENT TO THE COOK COUNTY OVERTIME POLICY RESOLUTION
(PROPOSED RESOLUTION AMENDMENT).
Submitting a Proposed Resolution
Amendment sponsored by Roberto Maldonado, County Commissioner.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Resolution Amendment.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION AMENDMENT
AMENDMENT TO THE
COOK COUNTY OVERTIME POLICY RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, there are legitimate reasons for overtime expenditures, es13eeially iR the areas ef
13liblie health aREI 13liblie safety such as providing adequate staffing to protect the public
health and safety when there exists a severe, protracted nationwide shortage of essential
licensed professionals to perfonn vital functions in the delive1y of government services; and
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
hereby establishes the following amended policy to guide overtime expenditures and to
protect the employees, patients, detainees and citizens of Cook County:
That all supervisors are required to provide a written report bi-monthly to their department
head relative to staffing needs. This report shall detail the number of vacancies and their
effect on operations as well as the expected overtime needs for the period of the report; and
That all department heads, bureau chiefs and elected officials immediately assign a
member(s) of their financi al team to oversee overtime expenses and that this individual(s),
along with an employee' s immediate supervisor, shall provide written authorization prior to
an employee being assigned or granted overtime; and

326 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

That this written authorization shall be forwarded to the department head, bureau chief and/or
elected official on a bi-monthly basis; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that no Cook County employee shall be allowed to work
more than 20 hours in overtime in any seven day period with the exception of emergency
situations where the bureau chief or elected official will be required to provide written
authorization; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that in any one fiscal year no Cook County employee shall
be allowed to work more than 624 hours (30% of 2080 full-time hours) in overtime with the
exception of emergency situations where the bureau chief or elected official will be required
to provide written authorization; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that in order to protect the public's basic human right to
quality health care, critical professional staffing positions in the Bureau of Health Services,
including, but not limited to, nurses, pharmacists, and radiology technicians, that are currently
experiencing a severe, protracted nationwide shortage of licensed professionals and
subsequently causing an unsafe patient to professional ratio, shall be exempt from the
requirements of this Resolution; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that these supervisors and managers are expected to adhere
to this policy and will be held accountable for unauthorized overtime expenditures within
their respective departments; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County's labor team is directed to address any
matters pertaining to overtime during the negotiating process and make recommendations that
ensure fairness to both the County's employees and taxpayers.
This amended policy shall go into effect immediately upon passage.
*Referred to the Health and Hospitals Committee on 07/12/05.
Commissioner Maldonado delivered the following overview of the Overtime Policy Resolution. The
Commissioners have extensive documentation that there is a severe shortage of certain types of health
professionals. The Resolution would exempt these individuals from the restriction of the twenty-hours
per week in overtime. The management prerogative of immediate supervisors and nurses would not be
usurped; if a nurse supervisor needs a nurse to work overtime she is able to ask that nurse to work
overtime without going through the administrative process. The requests to work overtime must come
from a supervisor.
Commissioner Hansen asked for further explanation of the need for overtime.
Dr. Winship replied that in his opinion the changes are not necessary; he has, however, no objection. This
Resolution addresses issues of emergency and urgency. Additionally, the Bureau has been decreasing its
use of overtime, and has extensive documentation of that this is effective.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired whether supervisors know how much overtime a given nurse has worked
and, also, why a nurse is punished for working overtime if her supervisor has asked her to work overtime.

3262

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

Dr. Winship replied that it is the supervisors' responsibility, not the nurses', to keep track of ove11ime.
He further stated that there are flaws in the letter submitted to the Commissioners; Mr. Brown has
instructed the supervisors not to use this letter.
Commissioner Peraica requested that the letter regarding the Executive Summary Recommendation from
the National Nurses' Organizing Committee, dated September 26, 2005, be entered into the record. (The
referenced document is on file in the Office of the County Clerk). He stated that the letter summarizes the
concerns that were part of the initial proposal. He further stated that he believes that certain leeway and
discretion should be granted to managers. He stated that the proposed amendments address this, and
suggested that the Committee approve these amendments.
Commissioner Maldonado moved approval of Communication No. 272043, seconded by

RESOLUTION DIRECTING THE CHIEF OF THE BUREAU OF HUMAN RESOURCES
AND THE CHIEF OF THE BUREAU OF HEALTH SERVICES TO CONDUCT AN
ANNUAL PHARMACIST SALARY SURVEY (PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting
a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Roberto Maldonado, County Commissioner; and Cosponsored by Peter N. Silvestri, County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the nationwide shortage of phannacists is a serious problem that threatens both
the quality of healthcare and access to health services; and
WHEREAS, since June 2004, pharmacists must obtain a Doctor of Phannacy Degree, known
as a Pharm.D., a six-year program requiring two years of prerequisite courses and four years
of phannacy school, before taking the licensing exam; and

3263

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005
WHEREAS, the increasing demand for pharmacists has caused a significant escalation in
wage rates attracting hospital pharmacists to leave their jobs for more lucrative positions in
the private sector; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Bureau of Health Services is facing critical challenges in its
pharmacy operations due to an obsolete salary structure and recruitment and retention
practices; and
WHEREAS, the Bureau of Health Services' failure to recruit a Phannacy Director,
supervisory staff and phannacists to fill twenty-four vacant positions has resulted in a
perilous patient to pharmacist ratio that will only worsen as the prescription volume continues
to soar beyond the estimated 3.8 million prescriptions to be dispensed in 2005 ; and
WHEREAS, although the Cook County Mail Order Pharmacy Refill Program has greatly
improved pharmacy service for our chronically ill patients, patients receiving short-tenn
prescriptions requiring immediate care still face unnecessary and sometimes dangerous
delays in receiving their prescription medications; and
WHEREAS, as one of the largest public health care networks in the country, the Bureau of
Health Services should serve as a leader in giving every patient the basic human right to
quality health care and treat them with the dignity and respect they deserve.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Human
Resources and the Chief of the Bureau of Health Services are directed to conduct an annual
Pharmacist Salary Survey, comparing the Bureau of Health Services' pharmacist salary rates
with those in the private sector, and to adjust the salary rate to reflect an average of those
rates found in the survey; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Health Services provide a
written report to the members of the Board of Commissioners on the phannacist salary
adjustment rate no later than one week prior to each fi scal year's budget presentation.
*Referred to the Health and Hospitals Committee on 07/12/05.

Commissioner Maldonado stated the following that by conducting an annual phannacy salary survey, the
County can compare the salaries of its phannacists to the phannacist salaries of other governmental
entities and to those of the private sector. The County currently has twenty-four vacancies; nine are line
phannacists who dispense prescriptions, seven are supervisors who do not dispense prescriptions pursuant
to union contracts, and one is a phannacy director. The County's salary for a new pharmacist is $70,000.
The Veterans Administration pays its new phannacists $8 1,300. The Veterans' Administration pays its
new phannacists $11,000 in additional salary, as compared to the County's salary.
Commissioner Peraica requested that when the Bureau of Health Services conducts then next survey they
also compare benefits packages.
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved the approval
Communication No. 272044. The motion carried.

RESOLUTION REGARDING PREPARATION OF A 48 HOUR PRESCRIPTION
Submitting a Proposed Resolution
DISPENSE PLAN (PROPOSED RESOLUTION).
sponsored by Roberto Maldonado, Jerry Butler, Forrest Claypool, Earlean Collins, John P.

PROPOSED RESOLUTION

TO PREPARE A 48 HOUR PRESCRIPTION DISPENSE PLAN
WHEREAS, patients utilizing pharmacy services at the Fantus Clinic and Stroger Hospital of
Cook County are often forced to wait up to fourteen days to receive their prescription
medications; and
WHEREAS, the situation worsens for patients utilizing the County's community health care
clinics with delays in receiving prescription medication sometimes extending to four weeks;
and
WHEREAS, these delays pose a serious threat to the public's health as a patient' s illness
may go untreated and they risk becoming more seriously ill; and

WHEREAS, the Bureau of Health Services expects to fill 3.8 million prescriptions in 2005
alone, averaging 10,000 prescriptions per day; and
WHEREAS, although the Cook County Mail Order Pharmacy Refill Program has greatly
improved pharmacy service for our chronically ill patients, patients receiving short-term
prescriptions requiring immediate care still face unnecessary and sometimes dangerous
delays in receiving their prescription medications; and

WHEREAS, as one of the largest public health care networks in the country, the Bureau of
Health Services should serve as a leader in giving every patient the basic human right to
quality health care and treat them with the dignity and respect they deserve.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Health Services
is directed to prepare a 48 Hour Prescription Dispense Pian outlining the steps the Bureau
will institute to ensure that all patients of the County's public health system will receive their
prescription medication within a 48 hour period; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Health Services provide a
written report to the Members of the Board of Commissioners within ninety days of
enactment of this Resolution.

272878

COOK COUNTY PRESCRIPTION RELIEF PROGRAM (PROPOSED RESOLUTION)
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Roberto Maldonado, County Commissioner;
and Co-Sponsored by John H. Stroger, Jr., President, Jerry Butler, Forrest Claypool, Earlean
Collins, John P. Daley, Elizabeth Ann Doody Gorman, Gregg Goslin, Carl R. Hansen, Joseph
Mario Moreno, Joan P. Murphy, Anthony J. Peraica, Mike Quigley, Peter N. Silvestri ,
Deborah Sims, Bobbie L. Steele and Larry Suffredin, County Commissioners.
I am submitting the following Resolution for the September 8, 2005 Board Agenda for
approval. The Resolution establishes a "Cook County Prescription Relief Program" in
partnership with MedAssist Direct, an Ohio Limited Liability Corporation .
The Cook County Prescription Relief Program is aimed at helping low income people who
have no prescription drug coverage receive their medications for a nominal cost. Although
Medicaid covers families with children, pregnant women, the elderly, and people with
disabilities, low income single individuals and married couples with no children under the
age of 65 are generally not eligible for government assistance and cannot afford private
health insurance. The Cook County Prescription Relief Program will seek to reach out to this
vulnerable population.
Under the program , MedAssist Direct helps participants access more than 1,800 prescription
medications available through pharmaceutical manufacturers for an annual enrollment fee of
$25.00. For a $7.00 per prescription transaction fee, MedAssist Direct completes and
processes the application and handles all the paperwork and necessary follow-up.
Participants receive their medications through the mail and save approximately 90% off the
average retail price on most prescriptions.
Aside from the costs of mailings, printing and distribution of appropriate marketing materials
infonning residents about the potential benefits of their enrollment in the program, there are
no other costs associated with the program.
The Cook County Prescription Relief Program can quickly and efficiently provide vital
savings to chronically ill, low income county residents with no prescription coverage.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Resolution.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, according to the 2000 Federal Census Bureau data, over 700,000 individuals in
Cook County live at or below the federal poverty income levels and many of them are
struggling to afford the cost of their prescription medications because they can neither afford
private health insurance nor do they qualify for government assistance programs such as
Medicaid; and
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
hereby adopts and approves this Resolution to enter into a marketing partnership agreement
with MedAssist Direct to offer the "Cook County Prescription Relief Program" to low
income residents of Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Bureau of Health Services shall present a
marketing plan for the Cook County Prescription Relief Program to the Board no later than
sixty days after the enactment of this Resolution; and

3268

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that after the marketing plan has been submitted, the
Bureau of Health Services has forty-five days to fully implement the Cook County
Prescription Relief Program.
*Referred to the Health and Hospitals Committee on 07/12/05.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner
Communication No. 272878. The motion carried.

THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, according to the 2000 Federal Census Bureau data, over 700,000 individuals in Cook
County live at or below the federal poverty income levels and many of them are struggling to afford the
cost of their prescription medications because they can neither afford private health insurance nor do they
qualify for government assistance programs such as Medicaid; and
WHEREAS, the majority of these uninsured or underinsured low income individuals, often unemployed
or working in low paying jobs, fai l to receive regular or preventive care and prescription drugs to treat
their illness, resulting in a higher incidence of disease, chronic illness, and disability; and
WHEREAS, the cost of caring for this vulnerable population often falls on the County' s public health
system which acts as a vi tal safety net provider of health care for the uninsured, poor and other patient
populations who may have no other recourse; and
WHEREAS, the growing population of the uninsured and underinsured in Cook County is creating an
overwhelming demand on the County 's public health system to dispense prescription medications; and
WHEREAS, in 2005 alone, the Bureau of Health Services expects to fill 3.8 million prescriptions,
averaging 10,000 prescriptions per day; and
WHEREAS, many phannaceutical manufacturers offer phannaceutical assistance programs that provide
free or low cost prescription medications to low income residents; and
WHEREAS, few residents are aware of the existence of these programs and even those who try to enroll
are overwhelmed by the complicated application process and fail to take advantage of the deep discounts
for their prescription medicines; and

3269

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

WHEREAS, residents without prescription coverage who have annual incomes of less than $19 ,000.00 if
they are single and less that $31,000.00 if they are married {approximately 200% above the federal
poverty income levels) are generally eligible to participate in such programs; and
WHEREAS, acting as an advocate for low income residents, MedAssist Direct works with local
governments, healthcare providers, community organizations, and individuals to promote awareness of
these programs and assist eligible residents to enroll and maintain their eligibility in pharmaceutical
assistance programs; and
WHEREAS, for an annual $25.00 enrollment fee, participants pay only $7.00 per prescription for each
30 day supply received from participating pharmaceutical manufacturers through the mail, saving
approximately 90% off the average retail price on most prescriptions; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners desires to relieve the burden of the high cost of
prescription drugs by enrolling our chronically ill, low income residents in these pharmaceutical
assistance programs; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners sees a significant benefit for our residents by
working with MedAssist Direct to promote awareness and enrollment in pharmaceutical assistance
programs; and
WHEREAS, other counties, communities, and organizations across America have successfully adopted
such programs and are currently providing assistance to those in greatest need; and
WHEREAS, the MedAssist Direct Phamrnceutical Assistance Program is modeled after an award
winning program, recognized by the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development and
the National Association of County Officials in 2004 as an exemplary health initiative to assist low
income residents; and
WHEREAS, as a home rule unit the Cook County Board has a legal mandate to provide for and protect
the health, welfare and safety of the residents of this County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners hereby
adopts and approves this Resolution to enter into a marketing partnership agreement with MedAssist
Direct to offer the " Cook County Prescription Relief Program" to low income residents of Cook County;
and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Bureau of Health Services shall present a marketing plan for
the Cook County Prescription Relief Program to the Board no later than sixty days after the enactment of
this Resolution; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that after the marketing plan has been submitted, the Bureau of Health
Services has forty-five days to fully implement the Cook County Prescription Relief Program.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of October 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

272879

COOK COUNTY PRESC RIPTION DISCOUNT CARD PROGRAM (PROPOSED
RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Roberto Maldonado,
County Commissioner. Co-Sponsored by John H. Stroger, Jr., President, Jerry Butler, Forrest
Claypool, Earlean Collins, John P. Daley, Elizabeth Ann Doody Gonnan, Gregg Goslin, Carl
R. Hansen, Joseph Mario Moreno, Joan P. Murphy, Anthony J. Peraica, Mike Quigley, Peter
N. Silvestri, Deborah Sims, Bobbie L. Steele and Larry Suffredin, County Commissioners.
l am submitting the following Resolution for the September 8, 2005 Board Agenda for
approva l. The Reso lution establishes a "Cook County Prescription Discount Card Program"
in partnership with the National Association of Counties (NACo). Aside from the costs of
mailings, printing and distribution of appropriate marketing materials infonning residents
about the potential benefits of their enrollment in the program, there are no other costs
associated with the program and no enrollment fees for the participants.
A lthough aimed at helping the uninsured and the underinsured with the high cost of their
prescriptions, the program is available to all of the residents of Cook County regardless of
age, income, or existing health coverage. The discount card is provided free of charge and
offers immediate discounts at participating pharmacies averaging 20 percent off the retail
price of commonly prescribed drugs.
Submitted is a sample contract between a part1c1pating county and the program 's
administrator as well as specific information about the program. A copy of the nearly 1,000
participating phannacies in Cook County is available for your review in my office as well as
any other additional infonnation you may need .
The Cook County Prescription Discount Card Program can quickly and efficiently provide
vital savings to county residents with no prescription coverage and can serve as an additional
safety net for those with limited coverage.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Resolution.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the National Association of Counties (NACo) has launched a prescription drug
discount card program aimed at helping chronically ill consumers cope with the high price of
prescription drugs; and
WHEREAS, administered by Advance PCS, a Division of Caremark Rx, Inc. of Nashville,
Tennessee, the card may be used by all county residents, regardless of age, mcome, or
existing health coverage; and
WH EREAS, the discount card is provided free of charge and offers immediate discounts at
participating phannacies averaging 14 percent off brand name medicine, 34 percent off
generic medicine, and 50 percent on select generics through mail service compared to regular
retail prices; and
WHEREAS, the discount card also covers medications excluded by some insurance
companies, such as birth control and smoking cessation treatments; and
WHEREAS, currently, there are 41 counties nationwide participating with NACo in this
prescription discount card program and 300 more are considering its benefits; and

327 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 5, 2005

WHEREAS, as a home rule unit the Cook County Board has the legal mandate to provide for
and protect the health, welfare and safety of the residents of this County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
hereby adopts and approves this Resolution to enter into a marketing partnership agreement
with the National Association of Counties (NACo) to offer the "Cook County Prescription
Discount Card Program" to all the residents of Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Bureau of Health Services shall present a Cook
County Prescription Discount Card Program marketing plan to the Board no later than sixty
days after the enactment of this Resolution; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that after the marketing plan has been submitted, the
Bureau of Health Services has forty-five days to fully implement the Cook County
Prescription Discount Card Program.

RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ROBERTO MALDONADO, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
